<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">GlaxoSmithKline</h1> <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div> <div id="contentSub"></div>

<p><b> GlaxoSmithKline plc</b> (<b>GSK</b>) is a British <a href="/wiki/Pharmaceutical_industry" title="Pharmaceutical industry">pharmaceutical company</a> headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Brentford" title="Brentford">Brentford</a>, London.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Established in 2000 by a <a href="/wiki/Mergers_and_acquisitions" title="Mergers and acquisitions">merger</a> of Glaxo Wellcome and SmithKline Beecham, GSK was the world's sixth largest pharmaceutical company as of 2015, after <a href="/wiki/Pfizer" title="Pfizer">Pfizer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Novartis" title="Novartis">Novartis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Merck_%26_Co." title="Merck &amp; Co.">Merck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hoffmann-La_Roche" title="Hoffmann-La Roche">Hoffmann-La Roche</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sanofi" title="Sanofi">Sanofi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[n 1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[4]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Emma_Walmsley" title="Emma Walmsley">Emma Walmsley</a> became <a href="/wiki/Chief_executive_officer" title="Chief executive officer">CEO</a> on 31 March 2017 and is the first female CEO of the company.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[5]</a></sup>
</p><p>The company has a primary listing on the <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange" title="London Stock Exchange">London Stock Exchange</a> and is a constituent of the <a href="/wiki/FTSE_100_Index" title="FTSE 100 Index">FTSE 100 Index</a>. As of August 2016 it had a market capitalisation of £81 billion (around $107 billion), the fourth largest on the <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> Stock Exchange.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[6]</a></sup> It has a secondary listing on the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">New York Stock Exchange</a>.
</p><p>GSK's drugs and vaccines earned £21.3 billion in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AR2013_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-AR2013-8">[7]</a></sup> Its top-selling products that year were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Advair" title="Advair">Advair</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Avodart" title="Avodart">Avodart</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flovent" title="Flovent">Flovent</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Augmentin" title="Augmentin">Augmentin</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lovaza" title="Lovaza">Lovaza</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lamictal" title="Lamictal">Lamictal</a>. GSK's consumer products, which earned £5.2 billion in 2013, include <a href="/wiki/Sensodyne" title="Sensodyne">Sensodyne</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aquafresh" title="Aquafresh">Aquafresh</a> toothpaste, the malted-milk drink <a href="/wiki/Horlicks" title="Horlicks">Horlicks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Docosanol" title="Docosanol">Abreva</a> for cold sores, Breathe Right <a href="/wiki/Nasal_strip" title="Nasal strip">nasal strips</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nicoderm" title="Nicoderm">Nicoderm</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nicorette" title="Nicorette">Nicorette</a> nicotine replacements, and Night Nurse, a cold remedy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GSKproducts_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-GSKproducts-9">[8]</a></sup> The company developed the first <a href="/wiki/Malaria_vaccine" title="Malaria vaccine">malaria vaccine</a>, <a href="/wiki/RTS,S" title="RTS,S">RTS,S</a>, which it said in 2014 it would make available for five percent above cost.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-malariavaccine_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-malariavaccine-10">[9]</a></sup> Legacy products developed at GSK include several listed in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization_Model_List_of_Essential_Medicines" title="World Health Organization Model List of Essential Medicines">World Health Organization Model List of Essential Medicines</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Amoxicillin" title="Amoxicillin">amoxicillin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercaptopurine" title="Mercaptopurine">mercaptopurine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pyrimethamine" title="Pyrimethamine">pyrimethamine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zidovudine" title="Zidovudine">zidovudine</a>.
</p><p>In 2012 GSK pleaded guilty to promotion of drugs for unapproved uses, failure to report safety data, and kickbacks to physicians in the United States and agreed to pay a $3 billion (£1.9bn) settlement. It was the largest health-care fraud case to date in that country and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_largest_pharmaceutical_settlements_in_the_United_States" title="List of largest pharmaceutical settlements in the United States">largest settlement</a> by a drug company.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USDOJJuly2012_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-USDOJJuly2012-11">[10]</a></sup>
</p>

<ul>
<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-18"><a href="#Overview"><span class="tocnumber">4.1.1</span> <span class="toctext">Overview</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-19"><a href="#Rosiglitazone_(Avandia)"><span class="tocnumber">4.1.2</span> <span class="toctext">Rosiglitazone (Avandia)</span></a></li>

</ul>
</li>
<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Antitrust_case_over_griseofulvin"><span class="tocnumber">4.2</span> <span class="toctext">Antitrust case over griseofulvin</span></a></li>
